Cross-Suite Summary — periodic-ci-openshift-release-main-nightly-5.0-e2e-telco5g-ptp


TL;DR: The WPC T-GM never achieved GNSS lock (clock class 248 throughout), cascading all 25 failures across every suite.



Root Cause Groups:


• 20/25 failures — GM stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248), cascading to all downstream sync assertions

All tgm (5), all dualfollower (3), and the majority of dualnicbc (≥6) and dualnicbcha (≥6) failures trace back to the WPC T-GM pod linuxptp-daemon-7g7z8 never advancing ts2phc/ptp4l to clock class 6 (GNSS LOCKED). With no locked grandmaster, every BC and slave node remained in LISTENING or FREERUN, causing 600-second Eventually timeouts on clock-state metrics that linuxptp-daemon only publishes after a port exits LISTENING state. The overall job also hit the 3h45m CI wall-clock timeout.


• 5/25 failures — pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET argument-splitting bug in conformance test helper

Three dualnicbc tests ("Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority") and two dualnicbcha tests ("Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master") failed with bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET. The pmc binary received the two-word command as two separate argv tokens and rejected each. This is an independent code regression in the ptp-operator conformance test helper's pmc invocation path — it would cause failures even if the GM were locked.



Cross-Suite Patterns:


Root Causedualfollowerdualnicbcdualnicbchatgm
GM FREERUN (clock class 248)All 3~6/9~6/8All 5
pmc arg-split bug—3/92/8—

• The GM FREERUN pattern is fully cross-suite — every suite has at least one failure directly asserting Expected : 248 to equal : 6. This rules out a per-suite or per-node flake.
• The pmc argument bug is isolated to the BC suites (dualnicbc, dualnicbcha) because only those suites issue GET PARENT_DATA_SET queries to identify parent clock identity.
• dualfollower and tgm have no suite-specific causes — both are purely downstream victims of the upstream GM failure.


Actionable Recommendations:


1. Investigate the T-GM GNSS lock failure first (highest leverage — blocks ~80% of failures). Check whether the rdu2 lab GNSS antenna/signal was degraded during the 2026-06-21 run window, and compare the ts2phc and linuxptp-daemon behavior between the last passing nightly and 5.0.0-0.nightly-2026-06-20-203914 on RHCOS 10.2.20260617-0 (kernel 6.12.0-211.7.1.el10_2.x86_64). Focus on pkg/daemon/daemon.go NMEA source handling and pkg/parser/ts2phc_parser.go holdover-exit logic for regressions on the new RHEL 10-based kernel.

2. Fix the pmc invocation in the conformance test helper (eliminates 5 deterministic failures). In the ptp-operator test code path that calls pmc for GetForeignClockID/GetBCMasterClockID (around test/conformance/serial/ptp.go:610), pass "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" as a single argument string — exec.Command("pmc", "-u", "-b", "0", "-f", configFile, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET") — rather than two separate tokens. Alternatively, pipe via stdin: echo "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" | pmc -u -b 0 -f .

3. Add a pre-suite GM health gate. Before any BC or follower suite begins, assert that the T-GM reports clock class 6 within a reasonable timeout (e.g., 5 minutes). If the GM is not locked, skip or abort the dependent suites with a clear infrastructure error rather than accumulating hundreds of seconds of timeouts per test.


Overall Issue Class: test_regression

(Primary: likely ts2phc/linuxptp-daemon regression on new RHCOS 10.2 kernel preventing GNSS lock; Secondary: confirmed code regression in pmc invocation path in the conformance test binary.)


Overall Severity: CRITICAL

(25/25 failures, 4/4 suites affected, job hit wall-clock timeout; no PTP synchronization validated in this nightly run.)




Per-Suite Details



dualfollower



Suite: dualfollower (3 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 3 dualfollower ClockSync tests timed out because the slave interfaces on cnfdf31 never achieved LOCKED state — the WPC TelcoGrandMaster itself was stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248), so no downstream device could synchronize.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: GM not locked → follower interfaces stuck in LISTENING/FREERUN (affects: all 3 tests)
• Evidence:

```

Test 1 & 2 (ptpconfig test-slave1):

no Follower port in expected LOCKED state for ptpconfig test-slave1 (node=cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, label="ptp/clock-under-test", slaveIfs=[ens2f0np0 ens2f3np3]). Per-interface results:

ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state, nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found, available op[...]


Test 3 (ptpconfig temp):

ens2f3np3: role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING)

ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state, nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found, available op[...]


From tgm suite (same cluster run, same job), confirming GM state:

Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM

Expected : false to be true

Expected : 248 to equal : 6


From ci-operator-build-log.txt — test step killed by overall timeout:

{"msg":"Process did not finish before 3h45m0s timeout","time":"2026-06-21T18:25:13Z"}

error: failed to execute wrapped command: exit status 127

```

• Root Cause: The WPC TelcoGrandMaster node remained in FREERUN state (ptp4l clock class 248, confirmed by simultaneous tgm-suite failures) throughout the entire test run. With the upstream GM not locked, ptp4l on the dualfollower slave node cnfdf31 could not proceed past LISTENING state on interfaces ens2f0np0 and ens2f3np3. Consequently, the openshift_ptp_clock_state metric for ens2f0np0 was never published by linuxptp-daemon (the daemon only emits this metric after ptp4l parses a clock-state event, which requires the port to advance past LISTENING — see pkg/metrics/exporter.go:UpdateClockStateMetrics and pkg/event/event.go:971). For ens2f3np3, the openshift_ptp_interface_role metric existed but showed LISTENING (role 5) rather than SLAVE (role 1). This cascade failure — GM FREERUN → slaves stuck in LISTENING → no LOCKED metrics — caused all three 600-second Eventually timeouts in test/pkg/ptptesthelper/ptptesthelper.go:93.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — the TGM failure (clock class 248) is the upstream blocker. The cluster ran OCP 5.0.0-0.nightly-2026-06-20-203914 on RHCOS 10.2.20260617-0 (kernel 6.12.0-211.7.1.el10_2.x86_64, first RHEL 10-based RHCOS); ts2phc or the WPC-GM linuxptp integration may have a compatibility regression on this kernel. All 4 suites (dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha, tgm) fail simultaneously, confirming a cluster-wide rather than suite-specific issue. The dualnicbc/dualnicbcha suites additionally show bad command: GET\nbad command: PARENT_DATA_SET from pmc, which is consistent with a linuxptp version incompatibility on RHCOS 10.2 (pmc interactive mode may behave differently on the new kernel/linuxptp build bundled in the 5.0 nightly). Likely narrowed to a regression in the release-5.0 ptp-operator Dockerfile's bundled linuxptp against RHCOS 10.2 kernel 6.12.
• Is it a flake? No — the simultaneous failure of all 4 suites (dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha, tgm) on the same job run, all showing GM or synchronization failure, indicates a systemic regression rather than a transient flake.
• Suggested Fix: Investigate whether the ts2phc / WPC-GM linuxptp binary built for release-5.0 operates correctly on RHCOS 10.2 (kernel 6.12); check if the OCP 5.0 nightly from 2026-06-20 introduced a kernel or hardware driver change that breaks IEEE 1588 PHC access. As a near-term step, re-run the same job against a prior nightly to bisect whether this is a nightly regression or a persistent release-5.0 incompatibility with RHCOS 10.2.

Suite Issue Class: infra_other

Suite Severity: HIGH


dualnicbc



Suite: dualnicbc (9 failures)


Suite TL;DR: The BC node's ptp4l never locked to the upstream grandmaster (clock class stuck at 248/FREERUN), and pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET commands returned bad command errors in all tests that queried parent clock identity, cascading into outage-recovery, events-framework, and metrics failures.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: pmc "bad command" — PARENT_DATA_SET query broken (affects: "Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority")
• Evidence:

```

parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

and for ptp4l.0.config:

```

grandmasterIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

• Root Cause: pmc responded with two separate bad command lines — one for GET and one for PARENT_DATA_SET. This is the exact pmc error output when the two-word command GET PARENT_DATA_SET is passed as two separate shell arguments (e.g., exec.Command("pmc", ..., "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET")). The linuxptp pmc binary treats each positional argument as an independent command token; passing them unquoted causes each word to be rejected as an unknown command. The test helper in ptp-operator-conformance-test/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go (referenced at lines ~606–610) invokes pmc to read parent clock identity, and this invocation incorrectly splits the command. The linuxptp-daemon's own RunPMCGetParentDS in pkg/pmc/pmc.go:294 correctly passes the full string as one argument (exec.Command("pmc", ..., cmdStr) where cmdStr = "GET PARENT_DATA_SET"), but the test code uses a different path. The cross-suite reproducibility (same error in dualnicbcha) confirms this is a code regression, not an infrastructure flake.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — requires examining the ptp-operator test/conformance/serial/ptphelper.go git history around the GetForeignClockID/GetBCMasterClockID functions; the candidate is a recent change to the pmc invocation helper in the test binary.
• Is it a flake? No — deterministic pmc argument-splitting bug.
• Suggested Fix: In the ptp-operator test helper that invokes pmc non-interactively, pass the full command as a single quoted argument: exec.Command("pmc", "-u", "-b", "0", "-f", configFile, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET"), not as two separate args. Alternatively, redirect via stdin: echo "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" | pmc -u -b 0 -f .

• Group 2: ptp4l BC stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248) (affects: "Verify clockClass when locking PTP source on dual NIC boundary clock", "BC clock class recovers to Locked after upstream link outage")
• Evidence:

```

Expected PMC clock class 6 for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config

Expected : 248 to equal : 6

```

and:

```

Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM

Expected : false to be true

```

Clock class 248 = ClockClassFreerun per pkg/protocol/type.go:16: ClockClassFreerun protocol.ClockClass = 248. The same symptom appears identically in dualnicbcha and tgm suites. The BC test node cnfdf32 (config test-bc-master1) never transitioned from FREERUN to LOCKED during the entire 2h+ test window.

• Root Cause: The BC's ptp4l never received valid sync from the upstream grandmaster, leaving it at clockClass 248. This is consistent with an infrastructure issue (GM unavailability or GNSS loss) compounded by the Group 3 role confusion: the BC's upstream port ens2f0np0 was observed as MASTER (see Group 3), meaning ptp4l elected itself as GM when no upstream source was found. Because the tgm suite also shows class 248 failures (a completely separate node/config), a shared infrastructure problem — the physical GM not advertising or GNSS degradation on this nightly run — is the most probable cause.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — likely infra flake; check GM/GNSS hardware status for the ptpcimno cluster on 2026-06-21.
• Is it a flake? Likely yes — infra-level GM unavailability is not deterministic.
• Suggested Fix: Verify the upstream GM (test-grandmaster ptpconfig) was operational and its GNSS signal was healthy; add a pre-flight check in the test suite that aborts with [SKIP] if the GM is not in class 6 before running BC sync tests.

• Group 3: Upstream port recovered as MASTER instead of SLAVE (affects: "The slave node network interface is taken down and up")
• Evidence:

```

ens2f0np0 should recover to SLAVE

Expected <*errors.errorString | 0xc000828640>:

incorrect role for ens2f0np0, role expected=1(SLAVE), role observed=2(MASTER)

```

From the XML BeforeSuite output: DiscoveredMasterInterfaces=[ens2f0np0] — this is the BC's slave-to-GM port.

• Root Cause: After the interface outage on ens2f0np0, ptp4l's BMCA saw no upstream grandmaster (already in FREERUN/class 248 per Group 2) and elected the BC's port as MASTER. When the link was restored, the 300 s test timeout expired before the GM's Announce messages arrived and forced ens2f0np0 back to SLAVE state. This is a direct downstream consequence of Group 2 (no GM lock).
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — infra-dependent (GM unavailable).
• Is it a flake? Yes — when the GM is healthy and the BC is locked, recovery works within the timeout window.
• Suggested Fix: Ensure GM is locked before running outage-recovery tests; or extend the recovery timeout to accommodate the case where the GM itself needs to re-announce after the BC's link is restored.

• Group 4: cloud-event-proxy consumer never received initial sync state (affects: "Should receive events after linuxptp-daemon pod restart", "[dualnicbc-parallel] Event based tests PTP Slave Clock Sync")
• Evidence:

```

timedout PushInitialValue, waiting for log in ns=ptp-event-framework-test pod=consumer,

looking for = Got CurrentState: ({.*})

```

and:

```

could not push initial event, err=timedout PushInitialValue, waiting for log in

ns=ptp-event-framework-test pod=consumer, looking for = Got CurrentState: ({.*})

```

• Root Cause: The cloud-event-proxy sidecar publishes a SyncStateChange event only when ptp4l transitions to LOCKED. Because the BC was in FREERUN throughout (Group 2), cloud-event-proxy never emitted a LOCKED event, so the consumer pod log never matched Got CurrentState: ({.*}) within the test timeout.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — downstream of Group 2.
• Is it a flake? Yes — appears when GM sync fails.
• Suggested Fix: Same as Group 2 (fix GM lock first); the event tests should prerequisite-guard on BC being in class 6 before starting.

• Group 5: Time sync metrics absent (affects: "PTP metric is present verifies on slave")
• Evidence:

```

Time metrics are not detected

Expected : # HELP cne_api_events_published Metric to get number of events published by the rest api

...

cne_api_events_published{address="/sync/ptp-status/clock-class",status="success"} 2

```

The metric endpoint returned publisher/event-count metrics but not the time-offset/sync-state metrics the test polled for.

• Root Cause: PTP time-sync metrics (e.g. openshift_ptp_clock_state LOCKED) are emitted only when ptp4l is in LOCKED state. With clock class 248 (FREERUN), those metrics never appeared within the 300 s window. The partial metric output proves the metric endpoint itself was alive; the missing metrics are the direct result

incorrect role for ens2f0np0, role expected=1(SLAVE), role observed=2(MASTER)

```

From the XML BeforeSuite output: DiscoveredMasterInterfaces=[ens2f0np0] — this is the BC's slave-to-GM port.

• Root Cause: After the interface outage on ens2f0np0, ptp4l's BMCA saw no upstream grandmaster (already in FREERUN/class 248 per Group 2) and elected the BC's port as MASTER. When the link was restored, the 300 s test timeout expired before the GM's Announce messages arrived and forced ens2f0np0 back to SLAVE state. This is a direct downstream consequence of Group 2 (no GM lock).
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — infra-dependent (GM unavailable).
• Is it a flake? Yes — when the GM is healthy and the BC is locked, recovery works within the timeout window.
• Suggested Fix: Ensure GM is locked before running outage-recovery tests; or extend the recovery timeout to accommodate the case where the GM itself needs to re-announce after the BC's link is restored.

• Group 4: cloud-event-proxy consumer never received initial sync state (affects: "Should receive events after linuxptp-daemon pod restart", "[dualnicbc-parallel] Event based tests PTP Slave Clock Sync")
• Evidence:

```

timedout PushInitialValue, waiting for log in ns=ptp-event-framework-test pod=consumer,

looking for = Got CurrentState: ({.*})

```

and:

```

could not push initial event, err=timedout PushInitialValue, waiting for log in

ns=ptp-event-framework-test pod=consumer, looking for = Got CurrentState: ({.*})

```

• Root Cause: The cloud-event-proxy sidecar publishes a SyncStateChange event only when ptp4l transitions to LOCKED. Because the BC was in FREERUN throughout (Group 2), cloud-event-proxy never emitted a LOCKED event, so the consumer pod log never matched Got CurrentState: ({.*}) within the test timeout.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — downstream of Group 2.
• Is it a flake? Yes — appears when GM sync fails.
• Suggested Fix: Same as Group 2 (fix GM lock first); the event tests should prerequisite-guard on BC being in class 6 before starting.

• Group 5: Time sync metrics absent (affects: "PTP metric is present verifies on slave")
• Evidence:

```

Time metrics are not detected

Expected : # HELP cne_api_events_published Metric to get number of events published by the rest api

...

cne_api_events_published{address="/sync/ptp-status/clock-class",status="success"} 2

```

The metric endpoint returned publisher/event-count metrics but not the time-offset/sync-state metrics the test polled for.

• Root Cause: PTP time-sync metrics (e.g. openshift_ptp_clock_state LOCKED) are emitted only when ptp4l is in LOCKED state. With clock class 248 (FREERUN), those metrics never appeared within the 300 s window. The partial metric output proves the metric endpoint itself was alive; the missing metrics are the direct result



Cross-Suite Summary — periodic-ci-openshift-release-main-nightly-5.0-e2e-telco5g-ptp


TL;DR: The WPC T-GM never achieved GNSS lock (clock class 248 throughout), cascading all 25 failures across every suite.



Root Cause Groups:


• 20/25 failures — GM stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248), cascading to all downstream sync assertions

All tgm (5), all dualfollower (3), and the majority of dualnicbc (≥6) and dualnicbcha (≥6) failures trace back to the WPC T-GM pod linuxptp-daemon-7g7z8 never advancing ts2phc/ptp4l to clock class 6 (GNSS LOCKED). With no locked grandmaster, every BC and slave node remained in LISTENING or FREERUN, causing 600-second Eventually timeouts on clock-state metrics that linuxptp-daemon only publishes after a port exits LISTENING state. The overall job also hit the 3h45m CI wall-clock timeout.


• 5/25 failures — pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET argument-splitting bug in conformance test helper

Three dualnicbc tests ("Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority") and two dualnicbcha tests ("Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master") failed with bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET. The pmc binary received the two-word command as two separate argv tokens and rejected each. This is an independent code regression in the ptp-operator conformance test helper's pmc invocation path — it would cause failures even if the GM were locked.



Cross-Suite Patterns:


Root Causedualfollowerdualnicbcdualnicbchatgm
GM FREERUN (clock class 248)All 3~6/9~6/8All 5
pmc arg-split bug—3/92/8—

• The GM FREERUN pattern is fully cross-suite — every suite has at least one failure directly asserting Expected : 248 to equal : 6. This rules out a per-suite or per-node flake.
• The pmc argument bug is isolated to the BC suites (dualnicbc, dualnicbcha) because only those suites issue GET PARENT_DATA_SET queries to identify parent clock identity.
• dualfollower and tgm have no suite-specific causes — both are purely downstream victims of the upstream GM failure.


Actionable Recommendations:


1. Investigate the T-GM GNSS lock failure first (highest leverage — blocks ~80% of failures). Check whether the rdu2 lab GNSS antenna/signal was degraded during the 2026-06-21 run window, and compare the ts2phc and linuxptp-daemon behavior between the last passing nightly and 5.0.0-0.nightly-2026-06-20-203914 on RHCOS 10.2.20260617-0 (kernel 6.12.0-211.7.1.el10_2.x86_64). Focus on pkg/daemon/daemon.go NMEA source handling and pkg/parser/ts2phc_parser.go holdover-exit logic for regressions on the new RHEL 10-based kernel.

2. Fix the pmc invocation in the conformance test helper (eliminates 5 deterministic failures). In the ptp-operator test code path that calls pmc for GetForeignClockID/GetBCMasterClockID (around test/conformance/serial/ptp.go:610), pass "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" as a single argument string — exec.Command("pmc", "-u", "-b", "0", "-f", configFile, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET") — rather than two separate tokens. Alternatively, pipe via stdin: echo "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" | pmc -u -b 0 -f .

3. Add a pre-suite GM health gate. Before any BC or follower suite begins, assert that the T-GM reports clock class 6 within a reasonable timeout (e.g., 5 minutes). If the GM is not locked, skip or abort the dependent suites with a clear infrastructure error rather than accumulating hundreds of seconds of timeouts per test.


Overall Issue Class: test_regression

(Primary: likely ts2phc/linuxptp-daemon regression on new RHCOS 10.2 kernel preventing GNSS lock; Secondary: confirmed code regression in pmc invocation path in the conformance test binary.)


Overall Severity: CRITICAL

(25/25 failures, 4/4 suites affected, job hit wall-clock timeout; no PTP synchronization validated in this nightly run.)




Per-Suite Details



dualfollower



Suite: dualfollower (3 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 3 dualfollower ClockSync tests timed out because the slave interfaces on cnfdf31 never achieved LOCKED state — the WPC TelcoGrandMaster itself was stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248), so no downstream device could synchronize.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: GM not locked → follower interfaces stuck in LISTENING/FREERUN (affects: all 3 tests)
• Evidence:

```

Test 1 & 2 (ptpconfig test-slave1):

no Follower port in expected LOCKED state for ptpconfig test-slave1 (node=cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, label="ptp/clock-under-test", slaveIfs=[ens2f0np0 ens2f3np3]). Per-interface results:

ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state, nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found, available op[...]


Test 3 (ptpconfig temp):

ens2f3np3: role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING)

ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state, nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found, available op[...]


From tgm suite (same cluster run, same job), confirming GM state:

Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM

Expected : false to be true

Expected : 248 to equal : 6


From ci-operator-build-log.txt — test step killed by overall timeout:

{"msg":"Process did not finish before 3h45m0s timeout","time":"2026-06-21T18:25:13Z"}

error: failed to execute wrapped command: exit status 127

```

• Root Cause: The WPC TelcoGrandMaster node remained in FREERUN state (ptp4l clock class 248, confirmed by simultaneous tgm-suite failures) throughout the entire test run. With the upstream GM not locked, ptp4l on the dualfollower slave node cnfdf31 could not proceed past LISTENING state on interfaces ens2f0np0 and ens2f3np3. Consequently, the openshift_ptp_clock_state metric for ens2f0np0 was never published by linuxptp-daemon (the daemon only emits this metric after ptp4l parses a clock-state event, which requires the port to advance past LISTENING — see pkg/metrics/exporter.go:UpdateClockStateMetrics and pkg/event/event.go:971). For ens2f3np3, the openshift_ptp_interface_role metric existed but showed LISTENING (role 5) rather than SLAVE (role 1). This cascade failure — GM FREERUN → slaves stuck in LISTENING → no LOCKED metrics — caused all three 600-second Eventually timeouts in test/pkg/ptptesthelper/ptptesthelper.go:93.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — the TGM failure (clock class 248) is the upstream blocker. The cluster ran OCP 5.0.0-0.nightly-2026-06-20-203914 on RHCOS 10.2.20260617-0 (kernel 6.12.0-211.7.1.el10_2.x86_64, first RHEL 10-based RHCOS); ts2phc or the WPC-GM linuxptp integration may have a compatibility regression on this kernel. All 4 suites (dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha, tgm) fail simultaneously, confirming a cluster-wide rather than suite-specific issue. The dualnicbc/dualnicbcha suites additionally show bad command: GET\nbad command: PARENT_DATA_SET from pmc, which is consistent with a linuxptp version incompatibility on RHCOS 10.2 (pmc interactive mode may behave differently on the new kernel/linuxptp build bundled in the 5.0 nightly). Likely narrowed to a regression in the release-5.0 ptp-operator Dockerfile's bundled linuxptp against RHCOS 10.2 kernel 6.12.
• Is it a flake? No — the simultaneous failure of all 4 suites (dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha, tgm) on the same job run, all showing GM or synchronization failure, indicates a systemic regression rather than a transient flake.
• Suggested Fix: Investigate whether the ts2phc / WPC-GM linuxptp binary built for release-5.0 operates correctly on RHCOS 10.2 (kernel 6.12); check if the OCP 5.0 nightly from 2026-06-20 introduced a kernel or hardware driver change that breaks IEEE 1588 PHC access. As a near-term step, re-run the same job against a prior nightly to bisect whether this is a nightly regression or a persistent release-5.0 incompatibility with RHCOS 10.2.

Suite Issue Class: infra_other

Suite Severity: HIGH


dualnicbc



Suite: dualnicbc (9 failures)


Suite TL;DR: The BC node's ptp4l never locked to the upstream grandmaster (clock class stuck at 248/FREERUN), and pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET commands returned bad command errors in all tests that queried parent clock identity, cascading into outage-recovery, events-framework, and metrics failures.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: pmc "bad command" — PARENT_DATA_SET query broken (affects: "Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority")
• Evidence:

```

parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

and for ptp4l.0.config:

```

grandmasterIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

• Root Cause: pmc responded with two separate bad command lines — one for GET and one for PARENT_DATA_SET. This is the exact pmc error output when the two-word command GET PARENT_DATA_SET is passed as two separate shell arguments (e.g., exec.Command("pmc", ..., "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET")). The linuxptp pmc binary treats each positional argument as an independent command token; passing them unquoted causes each word to be rejected as an unknown command. The test helper in ptp-operator-conformance-test/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go (referenced at lines ~606–610) invokes pmc to read parent clock identity, and this invocation incorrectly splits the command. The linuxptp-daemon's own RunPMCGetParentDS in pkg/pmc/pmc.go:294 correctly passes the full string as one argument (exec.Command("pmc", ..., cmdStr) where cmdStr = "GET PARENT_DATA_SET"), but the test code uses a different path. The cross-suite reproducibility (same error in dualnicbcha) confirms this is a code regression, not an infrastructure flake.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — requires examining the ptp-operator test/conformance/serial/ptphelper.go git history around the GetForeignClockID/GetBCMasterClockID functions; the candidate is a recent change to the pmc invocation helper in the test binary.
• Is it a flake? No — deterministic pmc argument-splitting bug.
• Suggested Fix: In the ptp-operator test helper that invokes pmc non-interactively, pass the full command as a single quoted argument: exec.Command("pmc", "-u", "-b", "0", "-f", configFile, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET"), not as two separate args. Alternatively, redirect via stdin: echo "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" | pmc -u -b 0 -f .

• Group 2: ptp4l BC stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248) (affects: "Verify clockClass when locking PTP source on dual NIC boundary clock", "BC clock class recovers to Locked after upstream link outage")
• Evidence:

```

Expected PMC clock class 6 for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config

Expected : 248 to equal : 6

```

and:

```

Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM

Expected : false to be true

```

Clock class 248 = ClockClassFreerun per pkg/protocol/type.go:16: ClockClassFreerun protocol.ClockClass = 248. The same symptom appears identically in dualnicbcha and tgm suites. The BC test node cnfdf32 (config test-bc-master1) never transitioned from FREERUN to LOCKED during the entire 2h+ test window.

• Root Cause: The BC's ptp4l never received valid sync from the upstream grandmaster, leaving it at clockClass 248. This is consistent with an infrastructure issue (GM unavailability or GNSS loss) compounded by the Group 3 role confusion: the BC's upstream port ens2f0np0 was observed as MASTER (see Group 3), meaning ptp4l elected itself as GM when no upstream source was found. Because the tgm suite also shows class 248 failures (a completely separate node/config), a shared infrastructure problem — the physical GM not advertising or GNSS degradation on this nightly run — is the most probable cause.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — likely infra flake; check GM/GNSS hardware status for the ptpcimno cluster on 2026-06-21.
• Is it a flake? Likely yes — infra-level GM unavailability is not deterministic.
• Suggested Fix: Verify the upstream GM (test-grandmaster ptpconfig) was operational and its GNSS signal was healthy; add a pre-flight check in the test suite that aborts with [SKIP] if the GM is not in class 6 before running BC sync tests.

• Group 3: Upstream port recovered as MASTER instead of SLAVE (affects: "The slave node network interface is taken down and up")
• Evidence:

```

ens2f0np0 should recover to SLAVE

Expected <*errors.errorString | 0xc000828640>:

incorrect role for ens2f0np0, role expected=1(SLAVE), role observed=2(MASTER)

```

From the XML BeforeSuite output: DiscoveredMasterInterfaces=[ens2f0np0] — this is the BC's slave-to-GM port.

• Root Cause: After the interface outage on ens2f0np0, ptp4l's BMCA saw no upstream grandmaster (already in FREERUN/class 248 per Group 2) and elected the BC's port as MASTER. When the link was restored, the 300 s test timeout expired before the GM's Announce messages arrived and forced ens2f0np0 back to SLAVE state. This is a direct downstream consequence of Group 2 (no GM lock).
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — infra-dependent (GM unavailable).
• Is it a flake? Yes — when the GM is healthy and the BC is locked, recovery works within the timeout window.
• Suggested Fix: Ensure GM is locked before running outage-recovery tests; or extend the recovery timeout to accommodate the case where the GM itself needs to re-announce after the BC's link is restored.

• Group 4: cloud-event-proxy consumer never received initial sync state (affects: "Should receive events after linuxptp-daemon pod restart", "[dualnicbc-parallel] Event based tests PTP Slave Clock Sync")
• Evidence:

```

timedout PushInitialValue, waiting for log in ns=ptp-event-framework-test pod=consumer,

looking for = Got CurrentState: ({.*})

```

and:

```

could not push initial event, err=timedout PushInitialValue, waiting for log in

ns=ptp-event-framework-test pod=consumer, looking for = Got CurrentState: ({.*})

```

• Root Cause: The cloud-event-proxy sidecar publishes a SyncStateChange event only when ptp4l transitions to LOCKED. Because the BC was in FREERUN throughout (Group 2), cloud-event-proxy never emitted a LOCKED event, so the consumer pod log never matched Got CurrentState: ({.*}) within the test timeout.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — downstream of Group 2.
• Is it a flake? Yes — appears when GM sync fails.
• Suggested Fix: Same as Group 2 (fix GM lock first); the event tests should prerequisite-guard on BC being in class 6 before starting.

• Group 5: Time sync metrics absent (affects: "PTP metric is present verifies on slave")
• Evidence:

```

Time metrics are not detected

Expected : # HELP cne_api_events_published Metric to get number of events published by the rest api

...

cne_api_events_published{address="/sync/ptp-status/clock-class",status="success"} 2

```

The metric endpoint returned publisher/event-count metrics but not the time-offset/sync-state metrics the test polled for.

• Root Cause: PTP time-sync metrics (e.g. openshift_ptp_clock_state LOCKED) are emitted only when ptp4l is in LOCKED state. With clock class 248 (FREERUN), those metrics never appeared within the 300 s window. The partial metric output proves the metric endpoint itself was alive; the missing metrics are the direct result

The test helper in ptp-operator-conformance-test/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go (referenced at lines ~606–610) invokes pmc to read parent clock identity, and this invocation incorrectly splits the command. The linuxptp-daemon's own RunPMCGetParentDS in pkg/pmc/pmc.go:294 correctly passes the full string as one argument (exec.Command("pmc", ..., cmdStr) where cmdStr = "GET PARENT_DATA_SET"), but the test code uses a different path. The cross-suite reproducibility (same error in dualnicbcha) confirms this is a code regression, not an infrastructure flake.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — requires examining the ptp-operator test/conformance/serial/ptphelper.go git history around the GetForeignClockID/GetBCMasterClockID functions; the candidate is a recent change to the pmc invocation helper in the test binary.
• Is it a flake? No — deterministic pmc argument-splitting bug.
• Suggested Fix: In the ptp-operator test helper that invokes pmc non-interactively, pass the full command as a single quoted argument: exec.Command("pmc", "-u", "-b", "0", "-f", configFile, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET"), not as two separate args. Alternatively, redirect via stdin: echo "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" | pmc -u -b 0 -f .

• Group 2: ptp4l BC stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248) (affects: "Verify clockClass when locking PTP source on dual NIC boundary clock", "BC clock class recovers to Locked after upstream link outage")
• Evidence:

```

Expected PMC clock class 6 for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config

Expected : 248 to equal : 6

```

and:

```

Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM

Expected : false to be true

```

Clock class 248 = ClockClassFreerun per pkg/protocol/type.go:16: ClockClassFreerun protocol.ClockClass = 248. The same symptom appears identically in dualnicbcha and tgm suites. The BC test node cnfdf32 (config test-bc-master1) never transitioned from FREERUN to LOCKED during the entire 2h+ test window.

• Root Cause: The BC's ptp4l never received valid sync from the upstream grandmaster, leaving it at clockClass 248. This is consistent with an infrastructure issue (GM unavailability or GNSS loss) compounded by the Group 3 role confusion: the BC's upstream port ens2f0np0 was observed as MASTER (see Group 3), meaning ptp4l elected itself as GM when no upstream source was found. Because the tgm suite also shows class 248 failures (a completely separate node/config), a shared infrastructure problem — the physical GM not advertising or GNSS degradation on this nightly run — is the most probable cause.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — likely infra flake; check GM/GNSS hardware status for the ptpcimno cluster on 2026-06-21.
• Is it a flake? Likely yes — infra-level GM unavailability is not deterministic.
• Suggested Fix: Verify the upstream GM (test-grandmaster ptpconfig) was operational and its GNSS signal was healthy; add a pre-flight check in the test suite that aborts with [SKIP] if the GM is not in class 6 before running BC sync tests.

• Group 3: Upstream port recovered as MASTER instead of SLAVE (affects: "The slave node network interface is taken down and up")
• Evidence:

```

ens2f0np0 should recover to SLAVE

Expected <*errors.errorString | 0xc000828640>:

incorrect role for ens2f0np0, role expected=1(SLAVE), role observed=2(MASTER)

```

From the XML BeforeSuite output: DiscoveredMasterInterfaces=[ens2f0np0] — this is the BC's slave-to-GM port.

• Root Cause: After the interface outage on ens2f0np0, ptp4l's BMCA saw no upstream grandmaster (already in FREERUN/class 248 per Group 2) and elected the BC's port as MASTER. When the link was restored, the 300 s test timeout expired before the GM's Announce messages arrived and forced ens2f0np0 back to SLAVE state. This is a direct downstream consequence of Group 2 (no GM lock).
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — infra-dependent (GM unavailable).
• Is it a flake? Yes — when the GM is healthy and the BC is locked, recovery works within the timeout window.
• Suggested Fix: Ensure GM is locked before running outage-recovery tests; or extend the recovery timeout to accommodate the case where the GM itself needs to re-announce after the BC's link is restored.

• Group 4: cloud-event-proxy consumer never received initial sync state (affects: "Should receive events after linuxptp-daemon pod restart", "[dualnicbc-parallel] Event based tests PTP Slave Clock Sync")
• Evidence:

```

timedout PushInitialValue, waiting for log in ns=ptp-event-framework-test pod=consumer,

looking for = Got CurrentState: ({.*})

```

and:

```

could not push initial event, err=timedout PushInitialValue, waiting for log in

ns=ptp-event-framework-test pod=consumer, looking for = Got CurrentState: ({.*})

```

• Root Cause: The cloud-event-proxy sidecar publishes a SyncStateChange event only when ptp4l transitions to LOCKED. Because the BC was in FREERUN throughout (Group 2), cloud-event-proxy never emitted a LOCKED event, so the consumer pod log never matched Got CurrentState: ({.*}) within the test timeout.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — downstream of Group 2.
• Is it a flake? Yes — appears when GM sync fails.
• Suggested Fix: Same as Group 2 (fix GM lock first); the event tests should prerequisite-guard on BC being in class 6 before starting.

• Group 5: Time sync metrics absent (affects: "PTP metric is present verifies on slave")
• Evidence:

```

Time metrics are not detected

Expected : # HELP cne_api_events_published Metric to get number of events published by the rest api

...

cne_api_events_published{address="/sync/ptp-status/clock-class",status="success"} 2

```

The metric endpoint returned publisher/event-count metrics but not the time-offset/sync-state metrics the test polled for.

• Root Cause: PTP time-sync metrics (e.g. openshift_ptp_clock_state LOCKED) are emitted only when ptp4l is in LOCKED state. With clock class 248 (FREERUN), those metrics never appeared within the 300 s window. The partial metric output proves the metric endpoint itself was alive; the missing metrics are the direct result



Cross-Suite Summary — periodic-ci-openshift-release-main-nightly-5.0-e2e-telco5g-ptp


TL;DR: The WPC T-GM never achieved GNSS lock (clock class 248 throughout), cascading all 25 failures across every suite.



Root Cause Groups:


• 20/25 failures — GM stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248), cascading to all downstream sync assertions

All tgm (5), all dualfollower (3), and the majority of dualnicbc (≥6) and dualnicbcha (≥6) failures trace back to the WPC T-GM pod linuxptp-daemon-7g7z8 never advancing ts2phc/ptp4l to clock class 6 (GNSS LOCKED). With no locked grandmaster, every BC and slave node remained in LISTENING or FREERUN, causing 600-second Eventually timeouts on clock-state metrics that linuxptp-daemon only publishes after a port exits LISTENING state. The overall job also hit the 3h45m CI wall-clock timeout.


• 5/25 failures — pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET argument-splitting bug in conformance test helper

Three dualnicbc tests ("Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority") and two dualnicbcha tests ("Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master") failed with bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET. The pmc binary received the two-word command as two separate argv tokens and rejected each. This is an independent code regression in the ptp-operator conformance test helper's pmc invocation path — it would cause failures even if the GM were locked.



Cross-Suite Patterns:


Root Causedualfollowerdualnicbcdualnicbchatgm
GM FREERUN (clock class 248)All 3~6/9~6/8All 5
pmc arg-split bug—3/92/8—

• The GM FREERUN pattern is fully cross-suite — every suite has at least one failure directly asserting Expected : 248 to equal : 6. This rules out a per-suite or per-node flake.
• The pmc argument bug is isolated to the BC suites (dualnicbc, dualnicbcha) because only those suites issue GET PARENT_DATA_SET queries to identify parent clock identity.
• dualfollower and tgm have no suite-specific causes — both are purely downstream victims of the upstream GM failure.


Actionable Recommendations:


1. Investigate the T-GM GNSS lock failure first (highest leverage — blocks ~80% of failures). Check whether the rdu2 lab GNSS antenna/signal was degraded during the 2026-06-21 run window, and compare the ts2phc and linuxptp-daemon behavior between the last passing nightly and 5.0.0-0.nightly-2026-06-20-203914 on RHCOS 10.2.20260617-0 (kernel 6.12.0-211.7.1.el10_2.x86_64). Focus on pkg/daemon/daemon.go NMEA source handling and pkg/parser/ts2phc_parser.go holdover-exit logic for regressions on the new RHEL 10-based kernel.

2. Fix the pmc invocation in the conformance test helper (eliminates 5 deterministic failures). In the ptp-operator test code path that calls pmc for GetForeignClockID/GetBCMasterClockID (around test/conformance/serial/ptp.go:610), pass "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" as a single argument string — exec.Command("pmc", "-u", "-b", "0", "-f", configFile, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET") — rather than two separate tokens. Alternatively, pipe via stdin: echo "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" | pmc -u -b 0 -f .

3. Add a pre-suite GM health gate. Before any BC or follower suite begins, assert that the T-GM reports clock class 6 within a reasonable timeout (e.g., 5 minutes). If the GM is not locked, skip or abort the dependent suites with a clear infrastructure error rather than accumulating hundreds of seconds of timeouts per test.


Overall Issue Class: test_regression

(Primary: likely ts2phc/linuxptp-daemon regression on new RHCOS 10.2 kernel preventing GNSS lock; Secondary: confirmed code regression in pmc invocation path in the conformance test binary.)


Overall Severity: CRITICAL

(25/25 failures, 4/4 suites affected, job hit wall-clock timeout; no PTP synchronization validated in this nightly run.)




Per-Suite Details



dualfollower



Suite: dualfollower (3 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 3 dualfollower ClockSync tests timed out because the slave interfaces on cnfdf31 never achieved LOCKED state — the WPC TelcoGrandMaster itself was stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248), so no downstream device could synchronize.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: GM not locked → follower interfaces stuck in LISTENING/FREERUN (affects: all 3 tests)
• Evidence:

```

Test 1 & 2 (ptpconfig test-slave1):

no Follower port in expected LOCKED state for ptpconfig test-slave1 (node=cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, label="ptp/clock-under-test", slaveIfs=[ens2f0np0 ens2f3np3]). Per-interface results:

ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state, nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found, available op[...]


Test 3 (ptpconfig temp):

ens2f3np3: role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING)

ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state, nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found, available op[...]


From tgm suite (same cluster run, same job), confirming GM state:

Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM

Expected : false to be true

Expected : 248 to equal : 6


From ci-operator-build-log.txt — test step killed by overall timeout:

{"msg":"Process did not finish before 3h45m0s timeout","time":"2026-06-21T18:25:13Z"}

error: failed to execute wrapped command: exit status 127

```

• Root Cause: The WPC TelcoGrandMaster node remained in FREERUN state (ptp4l clock class 248, confirmed by simultaneous tgm-suite failures) throughout the entire test run. With the upstream GM not locked, ptp4l on the dualfollower slave node cnfdf31 could not proceed past LISTENING state on interfaces ens2f0np0 and ens2f3np3. Consequently, the openshift_ptp_clock_state metric for ens2f0np0 was never published by linuxptp-daemon (the daemon only emits this metric after ptp4l parses a clock-state event, which requires the port to advance past LISTENING — see pkg/metrics/exporter.go:UpdateClockStateMetrics and pkg/event/event.go:971). For ens2f3np3, the openshift_ptp_interface_role metric existed but showed LISTENING (role 5) rather than SLAVE (role 1). This cascade failure — GM FREERUN → slaves stuck in LISTENING → no LOCKED metrics — caused all three 600-second Eventually timeouts in test/pkg/ptptesthelper/ptptesthelper.go:93.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — the TGM failure (clock class 248) is the upstream blocker. The cluster ran OCP 5.0.0-0.nightly-2026-06-20-203914 on RHCOS 10.2.20260617-0 (kernel 6.12.0-211.7.1.el10_2.x86_64, first RHEL 10-based RHCOS); ts2phc or the WPC-GM linuxptp integration may have a compatibility regression on this kernel. All 4 suites (dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha, tgm) fail simultaneously, confirming a cluster-wide rather than suite-specific issue. The dualnicbc/dualnicbcha suites additionally show bad command: GET\nbad command: PARENT_DATA_SET from pmc, which is consistent with a linuxptp version incompatibility on RHCOS 10.2 (pmc interactive mode may behave differently on the new kernel/linuxptp build bundled in the 5.0 nightly). Likely narrowed to a regression in the release-5.0 ptp-operator Dockerfile's bundled linuxptp against RHCOS 10.2 kernel 6.12.
• Is it a flake? No — the simultaneous failure of all 4 suites (dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha, tgm) on the same job run, all showing GM or synchronization failure, indicates a systemic regression rather than a transient flake.
• Suggested Fix: Investigate whether the ts2phc / WPC-GM linuxptp binary built for release-5.0 operates correctly on RHCOS 10.2 (kernel 6.12); check if the OCP 5.0 nightly from 2026-06-20 introduced a kernel or hardware driver change that breaks IEEE 1588 PHC access. As a near-term step, re-run the same job against a prior nightly to bisect whether this is a nightly regression or a persistent release-5.0 incompatibility with RHCOS 10.2.

Suite Issue Class: infra_other

Suite Severity: HIGH


dualnicbc



Suite: dualnicbc (9 failures)


Suite TL;DR: The BC node's ptp4l never locked to the upstream grandmaster (clock class stuck at 248/FREERUN), and pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET commands returned bad command errors in all tests that queried parent clock identity, cascading into outage-recovery, events-framework, and metrics failures.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: pmc "bad command" — PARENT_DATA_SET query broken (affects: "Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority")
• Evidence:

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

and for ptp4l.0.config:

```

grandmasterIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

• Root Cause: pmc responded with two separate bad command lines — one for GET and one for PARENT_DATA_SET. This is the exact pmc error output when the two-word command GET PARENT_DATA_SET is passed as two separate shell arguments (e.g., exec.Command("pmc", ..., "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET")). The cluster ran OCP 5.0.0-0.nightly-2026-06-20-203914 on RHCOS 10.2.20260617-0 (kernel 6.12.0-211.7.1.el10_2.x86_64, first RHEL 10-based RHCOS); ts2phc or the WPC-GM linuxptp integration may have a compatibility regression on this kernel. All 4 suites (dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha, tgm) fail simultaneously, confirming a cluster-wide rather than suite-specific issue. The dualnicbc/dualnicbcha suites additionally show bad command: GET\nbad command: PARENT_DATA_SET from pmc, which is consistent with a linuxptp version incompatibility on RHCOS 10.2 (pmc interactive mode may behave differently on the new kernel/linuxptp build bundled in the 5.0 nightly). Likely narrowed to a regression in the release-5.0 ptp-operator Dockerfile's bundled linuxptp against RHCOS 10.2 kernel 6.12.
• Is it a flake? No — the simultaneous failure of all 4 suites (dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha, tgm) on the same job run, all showing GM or synchronization failure, indicates a systemic regression rather than a transient flake.
• Suggested Fix: Investigate whether the ts2phc / WPC-GM linuxptp binary built for release-5.0 operates correctly on RHCOS 10.2 (kernel 6.12); check if the OCP 5.0 nightly from 2026-06-20 introduced a kernel or hardware driver change that breaks IEEE 1588 PHC access. As a near-term step, re-run the same job against a prior nightly to bisect whether this is a nightly regression or a persistent release-5.0 incompatibility with RHCOS 10.2.

Suite Issue Class: infra_other

Suite Severity: HIGH


dualnicbc



Suite: dualnicbc (9 failures)


Suite TL;DR: The BC node's ptp4l never locked to the upstream grandmaster (clock class stuck at 248/FREERUN), and pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET commands returned bad command errors in all tests that queried parent clock identity, cascading into outage-recovery, events-framework, and metrics failures.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: pmc "bad command" — PARENT_DATA_SET query broken (affects: "Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority")
• Evidence:

```

parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

and for ptp4l.0.config:

```

grandmasterIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

• Root Cause: pmc responded with two separate bad command lines — one for GET and one for PARENT_DATA_SET. This is the exact pmc error output when the two-word command GET PARENT_DATA_SET is passed as two separate shell arguments (e.g., exec.Command("pmc", ..., "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET")). The linuxptp pmc binary treats each positional argument as an independent command token; passing them unquoted causes each word to be rejected as an unknown command. The test helper in ptp-operator-conformance-test/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go (referenced at lines ~606–610) invokes pmc to read parent clock identity, and this invocation incorrectly splits the command. The linuxptp-daemon's own RunPMCGetParentDS in pkg/pmc/pmc.go:294 correctly passes the full string as one argument (exec.Command("pmc", ..., cmdStr) where cmdStr = "GET PARENT_DATA_SET"), but the test code uses a different path. The cross-suite reproducibility (same error in dualnicbcha) confirms this is a code regression, not an infrastructure flake.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — requires examining the ptp-operator test/conformance/serial/ptphelper.go git history around the GetForeignClockID/GetBCMasterClockID functions; the candidate is a recent change to the pmc invocation helper in the test binary.
• Is it a flake? No — deterministic pmc argument-splitting bug.
• Suggested Fix: In the ptp-operator test helper that invokes pmc non-interactively, pass the full command as a single quoted argument: exec.Command("pmc", "-u", "-b", "0", "-f", configFile, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET"), not as two separate args. Alternatively, redirect via stdin: echo "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" | pmc -u -b 0 -f .

• Group 2: ptp4l BC stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248) (affects: "Verify clockClass when locking PTP source on dual NIC boundary clock", "BC clock class recovers to Locked after upstream link outage")
• Evidence:

```

Expected PMC clock class 6 for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config

Expected : 248 to equal : 6

```

and:

```

Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM

Expected : false to be true

```

Clock class 248 = ClockClassFreerun per pkg/protocol/type.go:16: ClockClassFreerun protocol.ClockClass = 248. The same symptom appears identically in dualnicbcha and tgm suites. The BC test node cnfdf32 (config test-bc-master1) never transitioned from FREERUN to LOCKED during the entire 2h+ test window.

• Root Cause: The BC's ptp4l never received valid sync from the upstream grandmaster, leaving it at clockClass 248. This is consistent with an infrastructure issue (GM unavailability or GNSS loss) compounded by the Group 3 role confusion: the BC's upstream port ens2f0np0 was observed as MASTER (see Group 3), meaning ptp4l elected itself as GM when no upstream source was found. Because the tgm suite also shows class 248 failures (a completely separate node/config), a shared infrastructure problem — the physical GM not advertising or GNSS degradation on this nightly run — is the most probable cause.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — likely infra flake; check GM/GNSS hardware status for the ptpcimno cluster on 2026-06-21.
• Is it a flake? Likely yes — infra-level GM unavailability is not deterministic.
• Suggested Fix: Verify the upstream GM (test-grandmaster ptpconfig) was operational and its GNSS signal was healthy; add a pre-flight check in the test suite that aborts with [SKIP] if the GM is not in class 6 before running BC sync tests.

• Group 3: Upstream port recovered as MASTER instead of SLAVE (affects: "The slave node network interface is taken down and up")
• Evidence:

```

ens2f0np0 should recover to SLAVE

Expected <*errors.errorString | 0xc000828640>:

incorrect role for ens2f0np0, role expected=1(SLAVE), role observed=2(MASTER)

```

From the XML BeforeSuite output: DiscoveredMasterInterfaces=[ens2f0np0] — this is the BC's slave-to-GM port.

• Root Cause: After the interface outage on ens2f0np0, ptp4l's BMCA saw no upstream grandmaster (already in FREERUN/class 248 per Group 2) and elected the BC's port as MASTER. When the link was restored, the 300 s test timeout expired before the GM's Announce messages arrived and forced ens2f0np0 back to SLAVE state. This is a direct downstream consequence of Group 2 (no GM lock).
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — infra-dependent (GM unavailable).
• Is it a flake? Yes — when the GM is healthy and the BC is locked, recovery works within the timeout window.
• Suggested Fix: Ensure GM is locked before running outage-recovery tests; or extend the recovery timeout to accommodate the case where the GM itself needs to re-announce after the BC's link is restored.

• Group 4: cloud-event-proxy consumer never received initial sync state (affects: "Should receive events after linuxptp-daemon pod restart", "[dualnicbc-parallel] Event based tests PTP Slave Clock Sync")
• Evidence:

```

timedout PushInitialValue, waiting for log in ns=ptp-event-framework-test pod=consumer,

looking for = Got CurrentState: ({.*})

```

and:

```

could not push initial event, err=timedout PushInitialValue, waiting for log in

ns=ptp-event-framework-test pod=consumer, looking for = Got CurrentState: ({.*})

```

• Root Cause: The cloud-event-proxy sidecar publishes a SyncStateChange event only when ptp4l transitions to LOCKED. Because the BC was in FREERUN throughout (Group 2), cloud-event-proxy never emitted a LOCKED event, so the consumer pod log never matched Got CurrentState: ({.*}) within the test timeout.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — downstream of Group 2.
• Is it a flake? Yes — appears when GM sync fails.
• Suggested Fix: Same as Group 2 (fix GM lock first); the event tests should prerequisite-guard on BC being in class 6 before starting.

• Group 5: Time sync metrics absent (affects: "PTP metric is present verifies on slave")
• Evidence:

```

Time metrics are not detected

Expected : # HELP cne_api_events_published Metric to get number of events published by the rest api

...

cne_api_events_published{address="/sync/ptp-status/clock-class",status="success"} 2

```

The metric endpoint returned publisher/event-count metrics but not the time-offset/sync-state metrics the test polled for.

• Root Cause: PTP time-sync metrics (e.g. openshift_ptp_clock_state LOCKED) are emitted only when ptp4l is in LOCKED state. With clock class 248 (FREERUN), those metrics never appeared within the 300 s window. The partial metric output proves the metric endpoint itself was alive; the missing metrics are the direct result



Cross-Suite Summary — periodic-ci-openshift-release-main-nightly-5.0-e2e-telco5g-ptp


TL;DR: The WPC T-GM never achieved GNSS lock (clock class 248 throughout), cascading all 25 failures across every suite.



Root Cause Groups:


• 20/25 failures — GM stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248), cascading to all downstream sync assertions

All tgm (5), all dualfollower (3), and the majority of dualnicbc (≥6) and dualnicbcha (≥6) failures trace back to the WPC T-GM pod linuxptp-daemon-7g7z8 never advancing ts2phc/ptp4l to clock class 6 (GNSS LOCKED). With no locked grandmaster, every BC and slave node remained in LISTENING or FREERUN, causing 600-second Eventually timeouts on clock-state metrics that linuxptp-daemon only publishes after a port exits LISTENING state. The overall job also hit the 3h45m CI wall-clock timeout.


• 5/25 failures — pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET argument-splitting bug in conformance test helper

Three dualnicbc tests ("Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority") and two dualnicbcha tests ("Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master") failed with bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET. The pmc binary received the two-word command as two separate argv tokens and rejected each. This is an independent code regression in the ptp-operator conformance test helper's pmc invocation path — it would cause failures even if the GM were locked.



Cross-Suite Patterns:


Root Causedualfollowerdualnicbcdualnicbchatgm
GM FREERUN (clock class 248)All 3~6/9~6/8All 5
pmc arg-split bug—3/92/8—

• The GM FREERUN pattern is fully cross-suite — every suite has at least one failure directly asserting Expected : 248 to equal : 6. This rules out a per-suite or per-node flake.
• The pmc argument bug is isolated to the BC suites (dualnicbc, dualnicbcha) because only those suites issue GET PARENT_DATA_SET queries to identify parent clock identity.
• dualfollower and tgm have no suite-specific causes — both are purely downstream victims of the upstream GM failure.


Actionable Recommendations:


1. Investigate the T-GM GNSS lock failure first (highest leverage — blocks ~80% of failures). Check whether the rdu2 lab GNSS antenna/signal was degraded during the 2026-06-21 run window, and compare the ts2phc and linuxptp-daemon behavior between the last passing nightly and 5.0.0-0.nightly-2026-06-20-203914 on RHCOS 10.2.20260617-0 (kernel 6.12.0-211.7.1.el10_2.x86_64). Focus on pkg/daemon/daemon.go NMEA source handling and pkg/parser/ts2phc_parser.go holdover-exit logic for regressions on the new RHEL 10-based kernel.

2. Fix the pmc invocation in the conformance test helper (eliminates 5 deterministic failures). In the ptp-operator test code path that calls pmc for GetForeignClockID/GetBCMasterClockID (around test/conformance/serial/ptp.go:610), pass "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" as a single argument string — exec.Command("pmc", "-u", "-b", "0", "-f", configFile, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET") — rather than two separate tokens. Alternatively, pipe via stdin: echo "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" | pmc -u -b 0 -f .

3. Add a pre-suite GM health gate. Before any BC or follower suite begins, assert that the T-GM reports clock class 6 within a reasonable timeout (e.g., 5 minutes). If the GM is not locked, skip or abort the dependent suites with a clear infrastructure error rather than accumulating hundreds of seconds of timeouts per test.


Overall Issue Class: test_regression

(Primary: likely ts2phc/linuxptp-daemon regression on new RHCOS 10.2 kernel preventing GNSS lock; Secondary: confirmed code regression in pmc invocation path in the conformance test binary.)


Overall Severity: CRITICAL

(25/25 failures, 4/4 suites affected, job hit wall-clock timeout; no PTP synchronization validated in this nightly run.)




Per-Suite Details



dualfollower



Suite: dualfollower (3 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 3 dualfollower ClockSync tests timed out because the slave interfaces on cnfdf31 never achieved LOCKED state — the WPC TelcoGrandMaster itself was stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248), so no downstream device could synchronize.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: GM not locked → follower interfaces stuck in LISTENING/FREERUN (affects: all 3 tests)
• Evidence:

```

Test 1 & 2 (ptpconfig test-slave1):

no Follower port in expected LOCKED state for ptpconfig test-slave1 (node=cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, label="ptp/clock-under-test", slaveIfs=[ens2f0np0 ens2f3np3]). Per-interface results:

ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state, nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found, available op[...]


Test 3 (ptpconfig temp):

ens2f3np3: role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING)

ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state, nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found, available op[...]


From tgm suite (same cluster run, same job), confirming GM state:

Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM

Expected : false to be true

Expected : 248 to equal : 6


From ci-operator-build-log.txt — test step killed by overall timeout:

{"msg":"Process did not finish before 3h45m0s timeout","time":"2026-06-21T18:25:13Z"}

error: failed to execute wrapped command: exit status 127

```

• Root Cause: The WPC TelcoGrandMaster node remained in FREERUN state (ptp4l clock class 248, confirmed by simultaneous tgm-suite failures) throughout the entire test run. With the upstream GM not locked, ptp4l on the dualfollower slave node cnfdf31 could not proceed past LISTENING state on interfaces ens2f0np0 and ens2f3np3. Consequently, the openshift_ptp_clock_state metric for ens2f0np0 was never published by linuxptp-daemon (the daemon only emits this metric after ptp4l parses a clock-state event, which requires the port to advance past LISTENING — see pkg/metrics/exporter.go:UpdateClockStateMetrics and pkg/event/event.go:971). For ens2f3np3, the openshift_ptp_interface_role metric existed but showed LISTENING (role 5) rather than SLAVE (role 1). This cascade failure — GM FREERUN → slaves stuck in LISTENING → no LOCKED metrics — caused all three 600-second Eventually timeouts in test/pkg/ptptesthelper/ptptesthelper.go:93.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — the TGM failure (clock class 248) is the upstream blocker. The cluster ran OCP 5.0.0-0.nightly-2026-06-20-203914 on RHCOS 10.2.20260617-0 (kernel 6.12.0-211.7.1.el10_2.x86_64, first RHEL 10-based RHCOS); ts2phc or the WPC-GM linuxptp integration may have a compatibility regression on this kernel. All 4 suites (dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha, tgm) fail simultaneously, confirming a cluster-wide rather than suite-specific issue. The dualnicbc/dualnicbcha suites additionally show bad command: GET\nbad command: PARENT_DATA_SET from pmc, which is consistent with a linuxptp version incompatibility on RHCOS 10.2 (pmc interactive mode may behave differently on the new kernel/linuxptp build bundled in the 5.0 nightly). Likely narrowed to a regression in the release-5.0 ptp-operator Dockerfile's bundled linuxptp against RHCOS 10.2 kernel 6.12.
• Is it a flake? No — the simultaneous failure of all 4 suites (dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha, tgm) on the same job run, all showing GM or synchronization failure, indicates a systemic regression rather than a transient flake.
• Suggested Fix: Investigate whether the ts2phc / WPC-GM linuxptp binary built for release-5.0 operates correctly on RHCOS 10.2 (kernel 6.12); check if the OCP 5.0 nightly from 2026-06-20 introduced a kernel or hardware driver change that breaks IEEE 1588 PHC access.
